commit 666bcd255b3414dfb3191d178bd9c3fdb0e248e0
Author: kellijohnson <kellifayejohnson@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Jul 15 13:13:34 2015 -0700

    Set the working directory upon exit to orginal directory in SS_RunJitter
    
    Users specify the directory to run the jitter iterations with the argument
    mydir, which is used with setwd(mydir) at the start of SS_RunJitter, but
    if this was not your working directory the function left the user in
    mydir. This was rather annoying, and thus the commit changes the
    working directory back to the working directory prior to calling
    SS_RunJitter. It will change back even if the function fails.

 1 file changed, 5 insertions(+), 2 deletions(-)

commit 5d4b6fec3979ad5521f54cee38131efb569235ef
Author: mstachur <megan.stachura@noaa.gov>
Date:   Tue Oct 13 14:16:51 2015 -0700

    Fixed stackpoly bug
    
    This fixes a bug in stackpoly that would give an error when you tried to
    make the plots with solid fill (instead of hashed). The ifelse()
    functions that were used before would give this error when x.hash was
    not specified: 'x' is NULL so the result will be NULL. This should fix

commit e82cb5c66b625259b1b9492a51221b47d4e286f0
Author: Ian Taylor <ian.taylor@noaa.gov>
Date:   Wed Mar 15 22:02:13 2017 -0700

    deprecate Francis-B for conditional age comps
    
    Reporting both Francis-A and Francis-B values data weighting value for
    conditional age-at-length comps was a source of confusion and the A
    method has outperformed B in simulation analyses so is now the only
    reported value by default. Francis-B can be requested with the input
    ShowVersionB=TRUE.

commit f36e5e4542f04bf85c9c2c75b414878b7e8bf2ae
Author: Watal M. Iwasaki <heavywatal@users.noreply.github.com>
Date:   Thu Feb 21 15:43:33 2019 +0900

    Fix duplication check in SS_readctl
    
    `paste0()` with `sep=` argument works in an unexpected way.
    E.g., `paste0('a', 'b', 'c', sep=',') ends in 'abc ', not 'a b c'.
    Duplication in lambda table has been checked with the strings
    concatenated by paste0, and it can result in false positive.
    E.g., rows (1,20,1,1,0) and (12,0,1,1,0) get marked duplicated.

 2 files changed, 4 insertions(+), 8 deletions(-)

Date:   Wed Apr 10 15:34:51 2019 -0700

    catch columns for season and fleet were backwards in SS_readdat for 3.30
    
    #year season  fleet catch catch_se
    season is column 2
    fleet is column 3
    I am guessing the mixup came from the hake dat file that only has a single
    season and a single fleet making it hard to distinguish between the two
    columns.

 1 file changed, 3 insertions(+), 3 deletions(-)

commit e6335fe7316ab790da9cc0b001c4189853ffcb0d
Author: kellijohnson <kellifayejohnson@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Apr 10 15:37:05 2019 -0700

    standard error of log catch is stored as one value per fleet
    
    The value is overwritten for every year of catch data specific to
    a given fleet. This is fine and the code works, but will not work
    when there is more than one standard error for a given fleet. I don't
    know if this would ever happen, but I wanted to include a check
    so that the function that reads in the data tells the user that
    the code should be changed.

 1 file changed, 4 insertions(+)

commit 7262875975e45f8bc1ff3ab67af20c917fc76022
Author: kellijohnson <kellifayejohnson@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Apr 19 04:39:46 2019 -0700

    Format 3.30 catch for output based on new i/o SS files for 3.30
    
    Catches are stored in the 3.24 format in the datlist.
    The dat file was being written but could not be read by SS v.3.30.
    The formatting change to the catch time series before writing
    to the disk now allows SS v.3.30 to run. This was tested on
    sablefish 2019 data.

commit 1aec9198fe8a8d5c9b159c0afc04e04965ee3e8b
Author: kellijohnson-NOAA <kelli.johnson@noaa.gov>
Date:   Tue May 14 07:40:37 2019 -0700

    fix: allow for matrix of Flimitfractions in forecast
    
    If mylist$Flimitfraction is negative, a matrix of years and limits
    will follow Flimitfraction. I use -999 to find the end of the matrix.
    Then, many i values are skipped over so that the matrix values are not
    wrongly put into other named values.
    
    The write forecast function then puts writes these numbers back to the
    file if Flimitfraction is negative.
    
    I don't predict that the changes will have any conflicts with other
    versions of SS.

 2 files changed, 12 insertions(+)

commit f38874995cff70a5c2430747d35486a584660843
Author: Chantel Wetzel <chantel.wetzel@noaa.gov>
Date:   Fri May 17 09:17:06 2019 -0700

    fix: modification to read and write out the catch section for 3.30 models
    
    This change rolls back some changes which had catches being formatted into a matrix form.  The matrix form prevented fleet specific se around catch.  Now catches are kept in 3.30 list form in the read and writing code.  This change requires users to use these functions across the same model version (read 3.30 and write 3.30). Users will not be able to read a 3.24 file and write it in 3.30 format.  If we think this is a needed option we will need to create some additional checks and switches.  However, since the transition executable will do this for users, I am not sure if we want to try to emulate this within r4ss.

commit 8b94b6ed90402301926e57676e213446a73eb19e
Author: Kelli Johnson <kelli.johnson@noaa.gov>
Date:   Fri May 31 08:37:59 2019 -0700

    fix: use convert.type in get.df for 3.30 data to get numeric values
    
    get.df in SS_readdat_3.30 was returning character values
    for numeric values. I first noticed this because I was trying to manipulate
    some composition data. The CPUE data didn't display this issue because
    SS_readdat converted some of those characters to numeric values.
    I tried for a more general fix that would simplify the code.
    
    convert.type is used by read.table to convert to logical, integer,
    numeric, or complex and only if those fail will it generate character
    values (or factors if as.is=TRUE)
    
    I checked against two 3.30 data files that the results of the resulting
    list were the same. I also went back in the history of the development
    branch to ensure that the age and length comps had always been imported
    as character values and that a recent change didn't create this problem.
